style="width:368px;max-width:368px"><div class="trow"><div class="theader">Overall Champions</div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:182px;max-width:182px"><div data-file-height="2016" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Aleksander_Aamodt_Kilde" title="Aleksander Aamodt Kilde">Aleksander Aamodt Kilde</a> became the first Norwegian to win an overall World Cup title since <a href="/wiki/Aksel_Lund_Svindal" title="Aksel Lund Svindal">Aksel Lund Svindal</a> in <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_FIS_Alpine_Ski_World_Cup" title="2008–09 FIS Alpine Ski World Cup">2008–09</a>.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:182px;max-width:182px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Federica_Brignone_Semmering_2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Federica_Brignone_Semmering_2010.jpg/180px-Federica_Brignone_Semmering_2010.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="225" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Federica_Brignone_Semmering_2010.jpg/270px-Federica_Brignone_Semmering_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Federica_Brignone_Semmering_2010.jpg/360px-Federica_Brignone_Semmering_2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="2000" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Federica_Brignone" title="Federica Brignone">Federica Brignone</a> became the first Italian to win an overall World Cup title since <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Tomba" title="Alberto Tomba">Alberto Tomba</a> in <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_FIS_Alpine_Ski_World_Cup" title="1994–95 FIS Alpine Ski World Cup">1994–95</a>.</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/International_Ski_Federation" title="International Ski Federation">International Ski Federation</a> (FIS) <b>Alpine Ski World Cup</b>, the premier circuit for <a href="/wiki/Alpine_skiing" title="Alpine skiing">alpine skiing</a> competition, began in January <a href="/wiki/1967_FIS_Alpine_Ski_World_Cup" title="1967 FIS Alpine Ski World Cup">1967</a>, and the <span class="nowrap">2019–20</span> season marked the 54th consecutive year for the <a href="/wiki/International_Ski_Federation" title="International Ski Federation">FIS</a> <a href="/wiki/FIS_Alpine_Ski_World_Cup" title="FIS Alpine Ski World Cup">World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> As it had every year since <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_FIS_Alpine_Ski_World_Cup" title="2006–07 FIS Alpine Ski World Cup">2006</a> (when the Sölden races were cancelled by a snowstorm), the season began in <a href="/wiki/S%C3%B6lden" title="Sölden">Sölden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> in October.  The season was supposed to end with the World Cup finals in March, which were to be held in <a href="/wiki/Cortina_d%27Ampezzo" title="Cortina d&#39;Ampezzo">Cortina d'Ampezzo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> for the first time since they began in <a href="/wiki/1992%E2%80%9393_FIS_Alpine_Ski_World_Cup" title="1992–93 FIS Alpine Ski World Cup">1993</a>, but the finals were cancelled due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Italy" title="COVID-19 pandemic in Italy">COVID-19 outbreak in Italy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As part of an effort to control the expansion of the World Cup circuit while fighting increased specialization, the city events were dropped this season, to be replaced by more parallel events at regular venues, while the Alpine combined was expanded.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>  Due to the recent dominance of slalom specialists in the Alpine combined races, the format for that discipline was changed this season. As was previously the case, the first run continued to be the speed discipline (with Super-G having the preference over downhill). However, instead of the slalom run starting in reverse order of finish in the speed run, which allowed the slalom specialists (who tended to be slower in the speed run) to tackle fresh snow for their slalom run, while the speed specialists had to face the more challenging rutted snow at the end of the day, the skiers in the slalom run now started in the same order as the finish of the speed run, with the leader after the speed run becoming the first to race on the fresh slalom course.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Parallel format was also changed to make the race more TV-friendly. Parallel races now began with one classic qualification run with a single competitor on the slope (which was shown in the live TV broadcast), after which the top 32 qualifiers by time advanced to the elimination phase of the main competition. The round of 32 used the current run and re-run format, so that each competitor got to start from each side, but from the round of 16 forward, there was only one run per race and a direct knockout system.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> However, the new format immediately became controversial, as making two giant slalom courses equal in a single-run format proved impossible, and both the first men's and women's parallel giant slalom races suffered from "the luck of the draw" becoming determinative—in the men's race, all eight round-of-16 matches were won by the racer on the same randomly-selected course, and in the women's race, 17 of 20 winners came from the same course.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In addition, a new sixth discipline—parallel events (which combined parallel giant slalom and parallel slalom in points distribution)—was introduced, joining downhill, Super-G, giant slalom, slalom, and combined. A small crystal globe was to be awarded to the winner.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 1 February 2020, then-women's World Cup overall leader (and 3-time defending champion) <a href="/wiki/Mikaela_Shiffrin" title="Mikaela Shiffrin">Mikaela Shiffrin</a>'s father Jeff suffered grave injuries in an accident, and Shiffrin immediately left the World Cup tour.  His injuries proved fatal, and Shiffrin remained off the tour for the rest of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Prize_money">Prize money</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2019%E2%80%9320_FIS_Alpine_Ski_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Prize money">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div>
<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;">

<tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 33%;text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">
<p><b>Top-5 men</b>
</p>
<table cellspacing="1" cellpadding="3" style="border:1px solid #aaa; font-size:86%;">

<tbody><tr style="background:#e4e4e4;">
<th style="border-bottom:1px solid #aaa; width:10px;">Rank
</th>
<th style="border-bottom:1px solid #aaa; width:200px; white-space:nowrap;"><i>after all 36 races</i>
</th>
<th style="border-bottom:1px solid #aaa; width:37px;"><a href="/wiki/Swiss_Franc" class="mw-redirect" title="Swiss Franc">CHF</a>
</th></tr>

<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist">
<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-18">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">GS was originally scheduled on 14 December, but switched with Slalom to 15 December  due to heavy snow on Friday. It was finally canceled after Slalom was canceled on 14 December due to strong wind and rescheduled on 15 December.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-19"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-19">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Slalom was originally scheduled on 15 December, then switched with GS to 14 December, but due to strong wind again re-switched on 15 December.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-21"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-21">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Super-G in <a href="/wiki/Val_Gardena" title="Val Gardena">Val Gardena/Gröden</a> on 20 December 2019, was postponed three times due heavy fog in mid-section. Official final results after 48 of 64 competitors in finish. Last 16 didn't start, again due to fog.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-25"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-25">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Canceled Downhill in <a href="/wiki/Val_Gardena" title="Val Gardena">Val Gardena/Gröden</a> on 21 December 2019 is rescheduled to <a href="/wiki/Bormio" title="Bormio">Bormio</a> on 27 December 2019.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-44"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-44">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Canceled Downhill in <a href="/wiki/Yanqing_District" title="Yanqing District">Yanqing</a> on 15 February 2020 is rescheduled to <a href="/wiki/Saalbach-Hinterglemm" title="Saalbach-Hinterglemm">Saalbach-Hinterglemm</a> on 13 February 2020.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-46"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-46">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Canceled Super-G in <a href="/wiki/Yanqing_District" title="Yanqing District">Yanqing</a> on 16 February 2020 is rescheduled to <a href="/wiki/Saalbach-Hinterglemm" title="Saalbach-Hinterglemm">Saalbach-Hinterglemm</a> on 14 February 2020.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-50"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-50">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Canceled Alpine Combined from <a href="/wiki/Hinterstoder" title="Hinterstoder">Hinterstoder</a> on 28 February 2020 is rescheduled on 1 March 2020.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-52"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-52">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Canceled giant slalom from <a href="/wiki/Val_d%27Isere" class="mw-redirect" title="Val d&#39;Isere">Val d'Isere</a> on 15 December 2019 is rescheduled to <a href="/wiki/Hinterstoder" title="Hinterstoder">Hinterstoder</a> on 2 March 2020.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-65"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-65">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Ladies' downhill in <a href="/wiki/Val_d%27Isere" class="mw-redirect" title="Val d&#39;Isere">Val d'Isere</a> was rescheduled from 21 to 22 December 2019 due to heavy snowfall, and was scheduled to be replaced by the alpine combined (cancelled) on 22 December 2019 due to tight schedule.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-74"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-74">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Canceled downhill from <a href="/wiki/Val_d%27Isere" class="mw-redirect" title="Val d&#39;Isere">Val d'Isere</a> on 22 December 2019 was rescheduled to <a href="/wiki/Bansko" title="Bansko">Bansko</a> on 24 January 2020.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-81"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-81">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Canceled giant slalom from <a href="/wiki/Maribor" title="Maribor">Maribor</a> on 15 February 2020 is rescheduled to <a href="/wiki/Kranjska_Gora_Ski_Resort" title="Kranjska Gora Ski Resort">Kranjska Gora</a> due to warm weather forecast.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-83"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-83">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Canceled giant slalom from <a href="/wiki/Maribor" title="Maribor">Maribor</a> on 16 February 2020 is rescheduled to <a href="/wiki/Kranjska_Gora_Ski_Resort" title="Kranjska Gora Ski Resort">Kranjska Gora</a> due to warm weather forecast.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-85"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-85">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Canceled downhill from <a href="/wiki/Rosa_Khutor_Alpine_Resort" title="Rosa Khutor Alpine Resort">Rosa Khutor</a> on 1 February 2020 is rescheduled to <a href="/wiki/Crans-Montana" title="Crans-Montana">Crans-Montana</a> on 21 February 2020.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
